Common guest molecules include small organic compounds such as aromatic hydrocarbons (e.g., benzene, naphthalene), alkyl chains, and neutral molecules like alcohols and amines. Biomolecules such as amino acids, peptides, and nucleotides can serve as guests in biological supramolecular assemblies. The specific interactions—hydrophobic effects, hydrogen bonding, electrostatic interactions, and π-π stacking—govern the affinity and selectivity of these guest molecules for their hosts.
